        }
        mr-issue-page[codeFont] {
          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;
          align-items: stretch;
          justify-content: flex-start;
          z-index: 200;
        }

        }

          width: 100%;

        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        <p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

VULNERABILITY DETAILS



<b class="line"><!---->VULNERABILITY DETAILS<!----></b>



<br>





With Runtime.queryObjects, the JS heap can be traversed by a Chrome DevTools Protocol client, allowing it to perform heap exploitation. This breaks an implicit security assumption that a CDP client can only modify and execute JS in the Isolate that the debugger is attached to. 



<span class="line"><!---->With Runtime.queryObjects, the JS heap can be traversed by a Chrome DevTools Protocol client, allowing it to perform heap exploitation. This breaks an implicit security assumption that a CDP client can only modify and execute JS in the Isolate that the debugger is attached to. <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Specifically, at least the arrayBufferConstructor_DoNotInitialize constructor is revealed, as well as an ArrayBuffer containing a pointer to the CommandLineAPIData struct, which contains function pointers. 



<span class="line"><!---->Specifically, at least the arrayBufferConstructor_DoNotInitialize constructor is revealed, as well as an ArrayBuffer containing a pointer to the CommandLineAPIData struct, which contains function pointers. <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





VERSION



<b class="line"><!---->VERSION<!----></b>



<br>





Node Version: v10.19.0



<span class="line"><!---->Node Version: v10.19.0<!----></span>



<br>





Operating System: Linux 5.13.0-27-generic Ubuntu 20.04.3 LTS



<span class="line"><!---->Operating System: Linux 5.13.0-27-generic Ubuntu 20.04.3 LTS<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





REPRODUCTION CASE



<b class="line"><!---->REPRODUCTION CASE<!----></b>



<br>





Leak of uninitialized memory: 



<span class="line"><!---->Leak of uninitialized memory: <!----></span>



<br>





* Open DevTools



<span class="line"><!---->* Open DevTools<!----></span>



<br>





* Enter queryObjects(Object)



<span class="line"><!---->* Enter queryObjects(Object)<!----></span>



<br>





* Store result as global variable (assumed to be temp1)



<span class="line"><!---->* Store result as global variable (assumed to be temp1)<!----></span>



<br>





* Enter cons = temp1.find(e=>e.name && e.name == "arrayBufferConstructor_DoNotInitialize");



<span class="line"><!---->* Enter cons = temp1.find(e=&gt;e.name &amp;&amp; e.name == "arrayBufferConstructor_DoNotInitialize");<!----></span>



<br>





* Enter buf = cons(0x1000)



<span class="line"><!---->* Enter buf = cons(0x1000)<!----></span>



<br>





* View uninitialized memory using buf



<span class="line"><!---->* View uninitialized memory using buf<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Control flow redirection: 



<span class="line"><!---->Control flow redirection: <!----></span>



<br>





* Open DevTools



<span class="line"><!---->* Open DevTools<!----></span>



<br>





* Enter queryObjects(ArrayBuffer)



<span class="line"><!---->* Enter queryObjects(ArrayBuffer)<!----></span>



<br>





* Find ArrayBuffer with length 16 that starts with what looks like a pointer, store as global variable (assumed to be temp1)



<span class="line"><!---->* Find ArrayBuffer with length 16 that starts with what looks like a pointer, store as global variable (assumed to be temp1)<!----></span>



<br>





* Enter new Uint32Array(temp1)[0] = 0x41414141



<span class="line"><!---->* Enter new Uint32Array(temp1)[0] = 0x41414141<!----></span>



<br>





* Enter new Uint32Array(temp1)[1] = 0x41414141



<span class="line"><!---->* Enter new Uint32Array(temp1)[1] = 0x41414141<!----></span>



<br>





* Enter queryObjects(ArrayBuffer) (the console log when this returns will trigger the dereference)



<span class="line"><!---->* Enter queryObjects(ArrayBuffer) (the console log when this returns will trigger the dereference)<!----></span>



<br>





* Crash with dereference of 0x4141414141414141: (If this is done instead with a pointer to a struct with a correct offset to code, that code will be run)



<span class="line"><!---->* Crash with dereference of 0x4141414141414141: (If this is done instead with a pointer to a struct with a correct offset to code, that code will be run)<!----></span>



<br>

NOTE



<span class="line"><!---->NOTE<!----></span>



<br>





This bug was reported as a Cloudflare Workers vulnerability initially, as they use Isolates to isolate workers from each other, but allow CDP connections (across the internet) to debug workers running on their edge. From my understanding, Cloudflare already reached out to the V8 team, who recommended that I submit this here.



<span class="line"><!---->This bug was reported as a Cloudflare Workers vulnerability initially, as they use Isolates to isolate workers from each other, but allow CDP connections (across the internet) to debug workers running on their edge. From my understanding, Cloudflare already reached out to the V8 team, who recommended that I submit this here.<!----></span>

I'm using the standard DevTools UI to do those steps, attached to Node. This also works in DevTools on a browser page. I attached a recording of the segfault, let me know if you need any more info. 



<span class="line"><!---->I'm using the standard DevTools UI to do those steps, attached to Node. This also works in DevTools on a browser page. I attached a recording of the segfault, let me know if you need any more info. <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The reproduction is just to demonstrate that it's a problem. The actual use case is that, if an application embeds V8 and then uses the debugger on a particular Isolate, a debugger connecting to it with CDP can do these things and compromise the process, which may include other Isolates or capabilities. Of course, CDP is expected to be able to control JS execution inside the Isolate, but this is a lot more trust than that.



<span class="line"><!---->The reproduction is just to demonstrate that it's a problem. The actual use case is that, if an application embeds V8 and then uses the debugger on a particular Isolate, a debugger connecting to it with CDP can do these things and compromise the process, which may include other Isolates or capabilities. Of course, CDP is expected to be able to control JS execution inside the Isolate, but this is a lot more trust than that.<!----></span>

I don't think we can quite say that

<br>

"a CDP client can only modify and execute JS in the Isolate that the debugger is attached to" is a valid expectation at this point in time, as we expect CDP clients to be trusted.



<span class="line"><!---->"a CDP client can only modify and execute JS in the Isolate that the debugger is attached to" is a valid expectation at this point in time, as we expect CDP clients to be trusted.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Furthermore, there is no strong guarantee that Isolates in the same process cannot affect each other. This went out of the window with Spectre.



<span class="line"><!---->Furthermore, there is no strong guarantee that Isolates in the same process cannot affect each other. This went out of the window with Spectre.<!----></span>

Turns out the solution is not trivial after all. Replacing v8::ArrayBuffer with v8::External is not feasible since in one case, we need the value to be writable, and in another case we need to store two values instead of just one. Using internal object fields has other problems.



<span class="line"><!---->Turns out the solution is not trivial after all. Replacing v8::ArrayBuffer with v8::External is not feasible since in one case, we need the value to be writable, and in another case we need to store two values instead of just one. Using internal object fields has other problems.<!----></span>

> I don't actually see from these two issues how you cross the Isolate boundary? 



<span class="line"><!---->&gt; I don't actually see from these two issues how you cross the Isolate boundary? <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





With these two exploits, an uninitialized memory leak and an attacker-controlled struct dereference followed by calling a function in the struct, we should be able to perform heap exploitation and execute shellcode as the V8 process. 



<span class="line"><!---->With these two exploits, an uninitialized memory leak and an attacker-controlled struct dereference followed by calling a function in the struct, we should be able to perform heap exploitation and execute shellcode as the V8 process. <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This is just an example - I haven't tried this, but I'm pretty sure this or something like this would work, it'd just be cumbersome to develop. So, we can prepare a series of JS functions that, when JIT compiled under certain assumptions, contain useful assembly gadgets, either at correct or at misaligned instruction addresses. Then, after ensuring they are JIT compiled, we can leak pointers to these gadgets by spraying the heap with references to the functions, and then doing the uninitialized memory leak. 



<span class="line"><!---->This is just an example - I haven't tried this, but I'm pretty sure this or something like this would work, it'd just be cumbersome to develop. So, we can prepare a series of JS functions that, when JIT compiled under certain assumptions, contain useful assembly gadgets, either at correct or at misaligned instruction addresses. Then, after ensuring they are JIT compiled, we can leak pointers to these gadgets by spraying the heap with references to the functions, and then doing the uninitialized memory leak. <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





After we have pointers to them, we can call these gadgets by creating, in an ArrayBuffer, a fake CommandLineAPIData struct containing the gadget pointer where console.log would be, and then leaking the address to that in the same way. Finally, we set the existing internal ArrayBuffer to that address and calling queryObjects. When queryObjects finishes and then calls console.log, it will instead call the gadget, which, if it ends in a ret, will do something unexpected and then return control back to us.



<span class="line"><!---->After we have pointers to them, we can call these gadgets by creating, in an ArrayBuffer, a fake CommandLineAPIData struct containing the gadget pointer where console.log would be, and then leaking the address to that in the same way. Finally, we set the existing internal ArrayBuffer to that address and calling queryObjects. When queryObjects finishes and then calls console.log, it will instead call the gadget, which, if it ends in a ret, will do something unexpected and then return control back to us.<!----></span>

*** Boilerplate reminders! ***



<span class="line"><!---->*** Boilerplate reminders! ***<!----></span>



<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.



<span class="line"><!---->Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.<!----></span>
